    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer16284159533097654701">As the creepy little town of Nightshade prepares to celebrate its 200th anniversary—on Halloween, of course—many of its paranormal residents are receiving mysterious blackmail letters. Psychic teen Daisy Giordano and her sisters set out to find out who is behind the threats. But launching an investigation isn’t easy for Daisy with her overprotective father watching her eve</span>
  <span id="freeText16284159533097654701" style="display:none">As the creepy little town of Nightshade prepares to celebrate its 200th anniversary—on Halloween, of course—many of its paranormal residents are receiving mysterious blackmail letters. Psychic teen Daisy Giordano and her sisters set out to find out who is behind the threats. But launching an investigation isn’t easy for Daisy with her overprotective father watching her every move. Though she’s is happy to have him back after the years he spent being held captive by an anti-paranormal group called the Scourge, Dad is having difficult time adjusting to home life—and the fact that his little girl is now a senior in high school. He even disapproves of Daisy’s boyfriend, Ryan. Can their relationship take the strain? <br /><br />And Daisy’s got even more on her plate: A talented amateur chef, she has won cooking lessons with celebrity chef Circe Silvertongue. After nosing around (with a little help from Circe’s pet pig), Daisy begins to suspect the temperamental chef’s secrets aren’t only in her ingredients. . . . <br /><br />The fourth installment in this favorite series is full of surprises and scares! <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText15526712281640144590" style="display:none">This was a YA paranormal story featuring witches and werewolves.<br><br>Daisy was an okay character and I felt quite sorry for her the way that her father was treating her. The pace in this was pretty slow though, and the book dragged because of it.<br><br>The ending to this was fairly happy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433066531i/15045433.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>6 out of 10</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/957622941" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/957622941?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica Morfi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica Morfi" href="/user/show/5510829-veronica-morfi">Veronica Morfi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer957622941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15823529484704342707">Rating: 4/5<br/><br/>Another great instalment in the Dead Is series by Marlene Perez. In this 4th book it's Halloween time. I love Halloween, even though we don't celebrate it in Greece, and I love books taking placing during that time. So, of course, Halloween in Nightshade is not an exception. This time around, a lot of Nightshade's resident are being blackmailed. And everyone of the blackmailer's victims is a paranormal. So once again Daisy is on the case. Trying to figure out who is blackmailing half </span>
  <span id="freeText15823529484704342707" style="display:none">Rating: 4/5<br /><br />Another great instalment in the Dead Is series by Marlene Perez. In this 4th book it's Halloween time. I love Halloween, even though we don't celebrate it in Greece, and I love books taking placing during that time. So, of course, Halloween in Nightshade is not an exception. This time around, a lot of Nightshade's resident are being blackmailed. And everyone of the blackmailer's victims is a paranormal. So once again Daisy is on the case. Trying to figure out who is blackmailing half of the town is not her only worry though. She is taking cooking lessons with a very demanding chef, her dad is back after six years and is in overprotective mode and her student counsellor seems like is out to get her.<br /><br />This was another fast and fun story about Nighstshade. We got to see more of our beloved characters and even met some new ones. We saw more of the Sourge, the organization after the paranormals, and learn a bit more about Nightshade's history and the mystery that is Lil, the prophetic jukebox.<br /><br />I had such a great time reading this. I loved the interactions between Daisy and her sisters. They are one of my favorite book families. Also, I love Ryan, Daisy's boyfriend he is adorable and Sam, her best friend. I've come to love them all after so many stories about them. <br /><br />All in all, this was fun. The mystery was a bit predictable as in the rest of the books, but still very entertaining. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15823529484704342707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97655047" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5417910983951333214">Yes, I love it. I actually adore these stories by Perez. I could not wait to get my hands on Dead is Just a Rumor! I couldn’t wait to start reading when I finally received a copy. In a couple hours, I was finished devouring it and totally satisfied to remain in love with the Dead is… series. <br/> I love the jukebox, Daisy, Ryan, Sam, Poppy…let’s just say, I am a fan of the characters. The dad I am a little iffy with, but maybe because I grew to love this family while he was missing. Does that make m</span>
  <span id="freeText5417910983951333214" style="display:none">Yes, I love it. I actually adore these stories by Perez. I could not wait to get my hands on Dead is Just a Rumor! I couldn’t wait to start reading when I finally received a copy. In a couple hours, I was finished devouring it and totally satisfied to remain in love with the Dead is… series. <br /> I love the jukebox, Daisy, Ryan, Sam, Poppy…let’s just say, I am a fan of the characters. The dad I am a little iffy with, but maybe because I grew to love this family while he was missing. Does that make me mean? <br />Things are not right in Nightshade. Halloween is creeping up on the town and a famous chef may be involved in a wicked scheme. In addition, there are people being blackmailed and Daisy intends to get to the bottom of the crime. With a nosey guidance counselor, an overprotective father, and question worthy cooking classes, Daisy has her hands full. Will she, her friends, and her sisters find out what has the town spooked?<br />How much more fun could a book be for the 12 plus crowd? I just love the laid back writing, the true to life characters, and the supernatural flare. This fun, mystical romp is fun for the whole family.<br /><br />I give Dead is Just a Rumor 4.5 STACKS!<br /><br />Patiently waiting for the next addition in the DEAD IS… series, I am STACKGirl, Shannan <br /><br />Dead is Just a Rumor is to released August 2010<br /><br />For more reviews, check out Girlsinthestacks.com<br /></span>

<div id="review_108181276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108181276" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2324650-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254535447p2/2324650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108181276?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2324650-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108181276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2580540049405025752">This is the fourth book in the Dead Is series and it is really good. I like Dead is Just a Rumour because it's short (it only takes a couple of hours to read) and it is really entertaining. I love mysteries and this series is just full of them.<br/><br/>Daisy is a protagonist that is actually really awesome. She's a typical teenager apart from the fact that she has psychic powers but other than that she is really relatable and you can't help but love her.<br/><br/>I love Dead is Just a Rumour because it's really li</span>
  <span id="freeText2580540049405025752" style="display:none">This is the fourth book in the Dead Is series and it is really good. I like Dead is Just a Rumour because it's short (it only takes a couple of hours to read) and it is really entertaining. I love mysteries and this series is just full of them.<br /><br />Daisy is a protagonist that is actually really awesome. She's a typical teenager apart from the fact that she has psychic powers but other than that she is really relatable and you can't help but love her.<br /><br />I love Dead is Just a Rumour because it's really light and breezy. There's a bit of suspense to keep you entertained and as I was reading it I found myself going through the pages so I could find out more.<br /><br />My only complaint is that it ended quite abruptly. Although, I have a feeling there could be a book after this one. Fingers crossed there is.<br /><br />If you like paranormal or you like mysteries then Dead is Just a Rumour is definitely worth a read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2580540049405025752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117664413" />
    <a title="Jessica at Book Sake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3503667-jessica-at-book-sake"><img alt="Jessica at Book Sake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293939321p2/3503667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117664413?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica at Book Sake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica at Book Sake" href="/user/show/3503667-jessica-at-book-sake">Jessica at Book Sake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117664413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14143815845071448439">Another fun read from the series, this book has probably been my favorite of them this far. Another mystery in the town of Nightshade always keeps things interesting. A few new characters make their way into the pages, but it mainly centers around the same ones we have met before. We get to venture a little more into the lives of the Gordano family and now that Dad is there the family is larger. The book isn’t a keep-you-guessing type of a thing, if you think about it enough, you have all the cl</span>
  <span id="freeText14143815845071448439" style="display:none">Another fun read from the series, this book has probably been my favorite of them this far. Another mystery in the town of Nightshade always keeps things interesting. A few new characters make their way into the pages, but it mainly centers around the same ones we have met before. We get to venture a little more into the lives of the Gordano family and now that Dad is there the family is larger. The book isn’t a keep-you-guessing type of a thing, if you think about it enough, you have all the clues to solve the mysteries on your own, but it’s more fun to just get lost in the book and have it spelled out for you. That’s what makes it such a fun read, nothing to take too seriously. While the major mystery of the book was solved, not everything tied up nicely at the end, so we can look forward to another book in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14143815845071448439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3014035379513477180">Eh, these are fun - like little bon bon treats. It only took a few pages to remember the characters and where we left off at the end of the third book. We find the Giordano sisters in fine form. Daisy is in her senior year, but having trouble with her dad, recently rescued from a 6-year captivity and now overprotective. He's got some reasons: someone is blackmailing the paranormal residents of Nightshade. Daisy is also involved with a cold case disappearance of the town matriarch's sister. Fun a</span>
  <span id="freeText3014035379513477180" style="display:none">Eh, these are fun - like little bon bon treats. It only took a few pages to remember the characters and where we left off at the end of the third book. We find the Giordano sisters in fine form. Daisy is in her senior year, but having trouble with her dad, recently rescued from a 6-year captivity and now overprotective. He's got some reasons: someone is blackmailing the paranormal residents of Nightshade. Daisy is also involved with a cold case disappearance of the town matriarch's sister. Fun as always - a smidgen of mystery, good sense of humor, light romance, and some fun supernatural elements make these treats. Yes, predictable, yes, this one didn't quite have the satisfying ending as usual, but a fun series for the Twilight crowd that likes a quick, lighter read.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120749458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4096243562420669244">- From Bookyurt.com - <br/><br/>I recently discovered this breezy little teenage paranormal detective series and quickly chomped through all four books. The latest installment, Dead is Just a Rumor, comes out this week (though releasing against Suzane Collin’s Mockingjay is not the best marketing move). Still, after you’ve torn through Mockingjay, if you find yourself depressed by the end, this series is the perfect antidote. These books are just fun – think the Scooby gang, or if Nancy Drew lived in a to</span>
  <span id="freeText4096243562420669244" style="display:none">- From Bookyurt.com - <br /><br />I recently discovered this breezy little teenage paranormal detective series and quickly chomped through all four books. The latest installment, Dead is Just a Rumor, comes out this week (though releasing against Suzane Collin’s Mockingjay is not the best marketing move). Still, after you’ve torn through Mockingjay, if you find yourself depressed by the end, this series is the perfect antidote. These books are just fun – think the Scooby gang, or if Nancy Drew lived in a town of paranormal denizens.<br /><br />Daisy is an amusing and instantly likable lead, and it’s nice to see a character who has actual relationships with her family and (somewhat) normal teenage issues to deal with. The paranormal side is for the most part refreshingly light-hearted, a pleasant change from the dark, gothic-style drama that’s everywhere in YA. The town of Nightshade does have plenty of secrets for Daisy to uncover, and her sleuthing is fun to watch. And while the mysteries may not be particularly scary (or terribly surprising), they are still thoroughly entertaining.<br /><br />In this installment Perez gives us some story lines that are clearly going to carry through into the next book, and leaves us with plenty of questions about exactly what The Scourge did to Daisy’s Dad. Next book, please!<br /><br />I can’t say it enough – this is a effervescent, upbeat series, and even if you have a pretty good idea of how the ending is going to turn out, it’ll keep you hooked. These books are just fun to read.<br /><br />Byrt Grade: A-</span>
  <a data-text-id="4096243562420669244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_94381941" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94381941" />
    <a title="CeJayCe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3304158-cejayce"><img alt="CeJayCe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461049154p2/3304158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94381941?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CeJayCe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CeJayCe" href="/user/show/3304158-cejayce">CeJayCe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94381941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12882416229841855498">The author doesn't go into depth about anything. She skips from plot point to plot point with no real description. The characters are like cardboard cutouts: lifeless. Everything they say sounds completely fake. I can never imagine real people talking the way Daisy and her friends talk. Its like Perez has completely forgotten what it was like to be a teenager and thinks this is what they really sound like.<br/>Her writing is subpar. That's part of the reason why her books are so short. I've heard the</span>
  <span id="freeText12882416229841855498" style="display:none">The author doesn't go into depth about anything. She skips from plot point to plot point with no real description. The characters are like cardboard cutouts: lifeless. Everything they say sounds completely fake. I can never imagine real people talking the way Daisy and her friends talk. Its like Perez has completely forgotten what it was like to be a teenager and thinks this is what they really sound like.<br />Her writing is subpar. That's part of the reason why her books are so short. I've heard the word "vanilla" applied to her books, and I think its a perfect fit. Nothing exciting ever happens. Daisy and Ryan never do more than light kissing. No real violence, despite the fact that Nightshade is full of vampires, werewolves, witches, etc.<br />And while discussing all the supernatural creatures in the town, why does anyone even bother to "hide" them anymore. Daisy acts as if its some big secret. Almost EVERYONE in town is SOMETHING! Yet Daisy tiptoes and whispers like people around her aren't using their powers like crazy. <br />As usual with the mystery, the reader knows the culprit way before Daisy does. She pretends she's this major teen detective, but all the information always falls right into her lap (usually way before she actually <i>gets</i> it). She never really has to DO anything. Its almost insulting how many clues and hints the author drops. But perhaps she has to since her main character is ridiculously slow. Not to mention she's not the least bit subtle. Even when other people are trying to be, she just blurts things out. Not everything needs to be clarified to the extent Daisy does it.<br /><blockquote>"I crossed to the desk and knelt next to her. 'Did you see a key anywhere?'<br />	'Nope,' she said. 'Why don't you, you know?' She crossed her arms and made a little blinky face, like the woman in the bottle in that old TV show.<br />	'I'm not a genie,' I said. 'But maybe I can use my psychic powers to open it.'"</blockquote><br />For anyone who isn't clear, she was talking to Sam, who obviously knows she isn't a genie and OBVIOUSLY meant for Daisy to use her psychic powers. Its lucky for Daisy that she's the one spying on people and not the other way around. All it would take to figure out any of Daisy's schemes would be a decent eavesdropper with the way she just blurts everything out.<br />And I must also note this shocking revelation Daisy came to when confronting the culprit. Please keep in mind this is AFTER she's already face-to-face with the blackmailer and finds out they're a member of the Scourge and they don't like paranormals and they're making up crap about the students to get them sent away. <br /><blockquote>"'Words have power,' I said. 'The power to hurt.'<br />[blanking out culprit's name]'s face grew animated. 'You understand, then.'<br />'You <i>want</i> to hurt other people? Your students? People who trusted you?' I couldn't believe it."</blockquote><br />Why, Daisy? Why can't you believe it? You just found out who the evil villain is in this whole stupid story and you can't believe they'd actually want to <i>hurt</i> people? How pathetically naive are you? What did you THINK they were trying to do?<br />Oh, wait! She gets dumber!<br /><blockquote>"I figured something out. 'You're going to sell the secrets to the Scourge, aren't you?'"</blockquote><br />Yes. Yes, Daisy. You did figure something out. You figured something out that any sensible person would've assumed the minute the blackmailer told you they <i>work for the Scourge</i>!<br />Has anyone else realized what an idiot Daisy is? I can't be the only person.<br />On a side note: The mermaid girl. She inherited her mermaid-ness from her mother's side, meaning her mother is also a mermaid. The blackmailer sends pictures of her with her tail out to her parents. Dad hits the roof. Parents decide to send her to boarding school. No opinions so far, that's just what happened.<br />Now opinions: If her mother is a mermaid, there is no way in HELL she didn't know her daughter was a mermaid. So why send her to boarding school for being a mermaid? Is it because the dad didn't know? If not, why isn't her mother sticking up for her? Why is her mother punishing the girl for being the same thing she is? Nothing about that little story makes any sense; A mermaid sending her daughter away for being a mermaid.<br />Ah. I'm ranting. Let me wrap this up.<br />2 stars. Light reading. If you read it, don't attempt to take it seriously. Probably best for middle school girls.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12882416229841855498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_208079972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208079972" />
    <a title="Shelley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3081722-shelley"><img alt="Shelley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420295300p2/3081722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208079972?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelley" href="/user/show/3081722-shelley">Shelley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=2010-release">2010-release</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208079972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1487246271935087080">*Rating* 3.0 starts<br/>*Genre* YA Paranormal<br/><br/>*Review* <br/><br/>Everywhere Daisy goes, trouble isn't that far behind her. <br/><br/>Dead is Just a Rumor is the fourth book in the Dead Is Series by Marline Perez. As usual, our protagonist and psychic Daisy Giordano is once again having to come to terms with yet another change and challenge in her life; the return of her father Rafe Giordano after 6 years of being held hostage by the dreaded and evil Scourge because he was researching the paranormal community.<br/> <br/>The Scourge</span>
  <span id="freeText1487246271935087080" style="display:none">*Rating* 3.0 starts<br />*Genre* YA Paranormal<br /><br />*Review* <br /><br />Everywhere Daisy goes, trouble isn't that far behind her. <br /><br />Dead is Just a Rumor is the fourth book in the Dead Is Series by Marline Perez. As usual, our protagonist and psychic Daisy Giordano is once again having to come to terms with yet another change and challenge in her life; the return of her father Rafe Giordano after 6 years of being held hostage by the dreaded and evil Scourge because he was researching the paranormal community.<br /> <br />The Scourge, you see, doesn't particularly like the paranormal community. In fact, it actually HATES the paranormal so much that its stated goals are to rid the world of each and every single one of them by any means necessary. Oohhhhhh, I’m skeered now and shaking in my boots!<br /><br />Anyway, ole Rafe doesn’t exactly like the fact that Daisy has grown up and isn’t his little girl any longer. She’s got herself a boyfriend; she works part time at Slims, she’s starting H.S. as a senior, and now she has some kick-ass psychic abilities that she didn’t have when he left. (She was 12 when he was kidnapped)<br /><br />In fact, old Rafe goes a little too far in protecting and keeping Daisy from being around Ryan while her mother and sisters Poppy and Rose tell Daisy to chillax and give him a chance to get back to normal. Call him the over bearing and easy to sway father who yes, we understand that you’ve been under the Scourges grasps for 6 years, but, life as we know it changes, and growing up happens whether you like it or not.<br /> <br />The town of Nightshade is an interesting place to live. There are vampires, werewolves, witches, banshees, telepaths/psychics, an invisible man (Slim), a haunted jukebox named Lil, and now mermaids. The so called norms understand they are outnumbered, but don’t seem to mind, although there are some that are easily swayed into taking on the paranormal community at the behest of the Scourge.<br /><br />This story takes place while Nightshade is celebrating its 200 year founding and of course, Samantha Devereaux, Daisy’s best friend, is leading the charge in an effort to make sure it’s the best party ever. Daisy, naturally, gets dragged into volunteering her cooking skills which she actually learned from her father. The celebration happens on Halloween and there is a big shindig surrounding that as well as the fact it’s once again going to be at Mrs. Wilder’s mansion and restaurant.<br /> <br />Then there are the usual and unusual mysteries that Daisy has to answer:<br /><br />1. Who is Circe Silvertongue really and why in the hell does she have a pig named Balthazar with her? Is she a witch, or a sorceress? Did she turn a man into a pig for revenge and spite or does she enjoy having her own bacon maker around her at all times? And, why does she offer cooking lessons to Daisy as part of a contest only to treat her as a second class citizen and embarrass her in front of her school mates and family?<br /> <br />2. Why does Lil the Jukebox hate Circe so much? Is the Jukebox really Lily, Mrs. Wilders long lost and missing sister who went missing after becoming engaged to Bam Meriwether? Is Daisy really going to put herself into harm’s way once again in order to find the answer to these questions?<br /> <br />3. Who is Beatrice Tray really and why is she pretending to be a H.S guidance counselor? Is she the person blackmailing the paranormal community? Does Tray recruit and spy on the kids for the dreaded Scourge? If so, who else is a member of the scourge and why hasn’t the council done a better job of screening applicants to the school and other places knowing they have a large paranormal community that is under the microscope for the Scourge?<br /><br />4. And, why is it that Daisy, at 17 years of age, is smarter than the entire council and chief of police combined when it comes to finding who the villains are? Just asking!<br /><br />Dead Is Just a Rumor is the next to last book in the Daisy Giordano story block with Dead Is Not an Option being the last book. I would recommend reading the books in order to get a better flow of information, and feel for how the writer grows her characters.<br /><br />Books with Daisy Giordano as the main character:<br />DEAD IS THE NEW BLACK <br />DEAD IS A STATE OF MIND <br />DEAD IS SO LAST YEAR <br />DEAD IS JUST A RUMOR <br />DEAD IS NOT AN OPTION<br /><br />There will be new books in the DEAD IS series! look for the DEAD IS spin-off, which will feature a new main character, Jessica Walsh. DEAD IS A BATTLEFIELD and DEAD IS A KILLER TUNE will be out in 2012.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1487246271935087080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110546621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15198919113091089015">The Gist<br/><br/> It’s Daisy’s senior year. She has an amazing boyfriend, an awesome best friend, loving sisters, and her dad is finally back! She assumes everything will be perfect from here on in. She couldn’t have been more wrong. Problem one: her dad. Though it’s great to have him back after all these years, he’s having problems adjusting. He treats Daisy like a twelve year old - like no time has passed since he’s been away. He rarely leaves the house, and gets worried easily, and worst of all, he al</span>
  <span id="freeText15198919113091089015" style="display:none">The Gist<br /><br /> It’s Daisy’s senior year. She has an amazing boyfriend, an awesome best friend, loving sisters, and her dad is finally back! She assumes everything will be perfect from here on in. She couldn’t have been more wrong. Problem one: her dad. Though it’s great to have him back after all these years, he’s having problems adjusting. He treats Daisy like a twelve year old - like no time has passed since he’s been away. He rarely leaves the house, and gets worried easily, and worst of all, he always gives Daisy’s boyfriend, Ryan, a hard time. And Daisy has no idea why. Problem two: Circe Silvertongue, famous cook extraordinaire. In a summer cooking competition Daisy placed in second and won eight cooking lessons with the famous cooking TV star. Daisy would have been thrilled…except Circe turns out to have a huge temper and an even bigger ego. Problem three: blackmail. Select members of Nightshade have been receiving blackmail with a red wax seal and no one has any clue as to who is to blame. To add to the confusion, the 200th anniversary of Nightshade’s founding is coming up – on Halloween of course – and Samantha has them all busy planning and decorating for the main event. As usual, Daisy is determined to do it all and solve a mystery in the meantime.<br /><br /><br />What We Think<br /><br />Reviewed by Dream Catcher<br /><br />To begin this review, I came up with a cheesy and extremely lame rhyme. Here it is… One, two, three, four! So many Dead books, give us more! Hahaha…yeah, that was pretty bad. But, thankfully this book was not. Out of all the books in the Dead is… series, I have to say this one is (probably) my favorite. The plot had many different parts to it, and Daisy had to deal with a lot of problems all at once, which made the overall idea a lot more interesting. Not only that, but the characters we all know and love from the previous books in the series are back, along with some surprising new additions. Such as…Daisy’s father (not too surprising after the end of Dead is So Last Year), Circe, and Circe’s pet pig Balthazar. New, but still quite interesting. What I really liked about this book was that I was always eager to read more. There were no slow points where I would put the book down and not come back to it for a while. Nope. I basically sat down and read it right through (not that hard, considering it was only 201 pages long). Another great thing: it kept me guessing. Nothing was too predictable. Marlene Perez kept you asking questions right up till she got to answer them for you. No predictability, but there was that AHA! moment you get right when you figured something out and are kind of proud of yourself. A good book can do that. The characters were another high point. You love the old ones just as much (Daisy, Ryan, Poppy, Sam, ect.) but you find that the new ones add something to the book. Something the book wouldn’t have if Perez only had the old characters. The only thing I didn’t like was how short it was. I kind of wish it could be a little longer. 201 pages isn’t tiny, but it isn’t a big book either. I finished it in a day and I wasn’t even rushing! Anyways, if you liked Dead is the New Black, Dead is a State of Mind, and Dead is So Last Year, you’re going to love Dead is Just a Rumor. There’s romance, there’s suspense, there’s mystery, and of course there’s paranormal weirdness (I mean, come on. It’s Nightshade!). It’ll keep you interested until the last of those 201 pages. Stay tuned for Marlene Perez’s next and final book in the Dead is… Series, Dead is Not an Option coming spring of 2011. <br /><br />Real Teen Rating~ B+ : Wait for Vacation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15198919113091089015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143881134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8513539528828874903">Quirky, fun fourth book in the "Dead Is" comic, paranormal, mystery series for teens<br/>	<br/>Halloween is always a big event in Nightshade, a small community running over with paranormal residents. But this year it is particularly huge, because it is the town's two-hundredth anniversary. The festive atmosphere is dampened, though, when many residents begin receiving blackmail letters and no one can figure out who is sending them. Daisy Giordano, whose psychic gifts include ESP and telekinesis, is determ</span>
  <span id="freeText8513539528828874903" style="display:none">Quirky, fun fourth book in the "Dead Is" comic, paranormal, mystery series for teens<br />	<br />Halloween is always a big event in Nightshade, a small community running over with paranormal residents. But this year it is particularly huge, because it is the town's two-hundredth anniversary. The festive atmosphere is dampened, though, when many residents begin receiving blackmail letters and no one can figure out who is sending them. Daisy Giordano, whose psychic gifts include ESP and telekinesis, is determined to solve this mystery, but she is hampered by her father. He was recently rescued from years of captivity at the hands of an evil group called the Scourge, whose mission is to wipe out all paranormal beings from the face of the earth. Now that Daisy's father is back with his family again, he is both emotionally scarred by his experience and extremely overprotective of his daughters--especially Daisy, who is younger than her two college-age sisters.<br /><br />In addition to trying to solve the blackmail mystery, Daisy is heavily involved with cooking lessons with celebrity chef Circe Silvertongue. When Daisy won the lessons as a prize, she had high hopes that they would be an exciting opportunity to advance her considerable cooking skills. But Circe treats Daisy more like a despised lackey than a talented student. Not only that, Circe's behavior in general is highly suspicious. It is obvious to Daisy that her mentor has magical talents, but what are they? And why would someone as famous as Circe want to hang out in Nightshade. What is she really up to?<br /><br />On top of all these events, Daisy is troubled with boyfriend problems, too. Her beloved Ryan is considering attending colleges far from Nightshade due to the advice of Nightshade High's new guidance counselor, and as a result, Daisy might lose him within the year.<br /><br />I've really been enjoying this series, and this book is no exception. Daisy is a wonderful heroine, and her boyfriend Ryan is a sexy and endearingly wholesome werewolf. There are repeat appearances of a cast of quirky, paranormal residents of the fascinating little town of Nightshade, some new villains to keep Daisy on her toes and, delightfully, we gain new clues about the history of the enchanted juke box at the local diner.<br /><br />Anyone who enjoys YA fantasy with a comic twist will love this book and the entire "Dead" series.<br /><br />Note for parents, teachers and librarians: This book is G-rated. There are no incidents of drinking, drugs or adolescent sex either on or offstage, and Daisy's family relationships are warm and loving.<br /><br />I grade the book as follows:<br /><br />Heroine - 5 stars<br />Subcharacters - 5 stars<br />Fantasy world-building - 4.5 stars<br />Writing - 5 stars<br />Mystery Plot - 3.5 stars for adult readers and older teens, 5 stars for younger teens<br />Romantic Subplot - 5 stars<br />Overall - 5 stars<br />Comment Comment | Permalink<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8513539528828874903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LUD9qjFznagQCVyNfS2yyb6onvqUWw8Sjc/vCi1VNFha4r+bUKOMRqGcfAStXSFuqcFxBP0zzIoWj7IglsqFOQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gDm7Go5E/1WcqA6ogqSxaUoTZy0wX/ymDMpWFQdxGpT3m/kr75Tuuy09LiFS1CLOXXqI01k3Pz6Xigs/vO6r9Q==')})
  }
